<li id="cite_note-146"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-146">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal" id="CITEREFLiepertPrevidi.2C_Michael2009">Liepert, Beate G.; Previdi, Michael (2009). <a class="external text" href="http://journals.ametsoc.org/doi/abs/10.1175/2008JCLI2472.1" rel="nofollow">"Do Models and Observations Disagree on the Rainfall Response to Global Warming?"</a>. <i>Journal of Climate</i>. <b>22</b> (11): 3156–3166. <a href="/wiki/Bibcode" title="Bibcode">Bibcode</a>:<a class="external text" href="http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2009JCli...22.3156L" rel="nofollow">2009JCli...22.3156L</a>. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1175%2F2008JCLI2472.1" rel="nofollow">10.1175/2008JCLI2472.1</a>. <q>Recently analyzed satellite-derived global precipitation datasets from 1987 to 2006 indicate an increase in global-mean precipitation of 1.1%–1.4% decade−1. This trend corresponds to a hydrological sensitivity (HS) of 7% K−1 of global warming, which is close to the Clausius–Clapeyron (CC) rate expected from the increase in saturation water vapor pressure with temperature. Analysis of two available global ocean evaporation datasets confirms this observed intensification of the atmospheric <a href="/wiki/Water_cycle" title="Water cycle">water cycle</a>. The observed hydrological sensitivity over the past 20-yr period is higher by a factor of 5 than the average HS of 1.4% K−1 simulated in state-of-the-art coupled atmosphere–ocean climate models for the twentieth and twenty-first centuries.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGlobal+warming&amp;rft.atitle=Do+Models+and+Observations+Disagree+on+the+Rainfall+Response+to+Global+Warming%3F&amp;rft.au=Previdi%2C+Michael&amp;rft.aufirst=Beate+G.&amp;rft.aulast=Liepert&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.issue=11&amp;rft.jtitle=Journal+of+Climate&amp;rft.pages=3156-3166&amp;rft.volume=22&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fjournals.ametsoc.org%2Fdoi%2Fabs%2F10.1175%2F2008JCLI2472.1&amp;rft_id=info%3Abibcode%2F2009JCli...22.3156L&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1175%2F2008JCLI2472.1&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-royal_society_misleading_arguments-244"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-royal_society_misleading_arguments_244-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-royal_society_misleading_arguments_244-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Royal Society (13 April 2005). "Letter from The Royal Society: A GUIDE TO FACTS AND FICTIONS ABOUT CLIMATE CHANGE: Misleading arguments: Many scientists do not think that climate change is a problem. Some scientists have signed petitions stating that climate change is not a problem. ... There are some individuals and organisations, some of which are funded by the US oil industry, that seek to undermine the science of climate change and the work of the IPCC. They appear motivated in their arguments by opposition to the United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change and the Kyoto Protocol, which seek urgent action to tackle climate change through a reduction in greenhouse gas emissions.". <a class="external text" href="https://publications.parliament.uk/pa/ld200506/ldselect/ldeconaf/12/12we24.htm" rel="nofollow"><i>Economic Affairs – Written Evidence</i></a>. <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.giss.nasa.gov/" rel="nofollow">NASA Goddard Institute for Space Studies</a> – Global change research</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.ncdc.noaa.gov/sotc" rel="nofollow">NOAA State of the Climate Report</a> – U.S. and global monthly state of the climate reports</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://dels.nas.edu/Climate/Climate-Change/Reports-Academies-Findings" rel="nofollow">Climate Change at the National Academies</a> – repository for reports</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.nature.com/nclimate/index.html" rel="nofollow">Nature Reports Climate Change</a> – free-access web resource</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.metoffice.gov.uk/climate-guide" rel="nofollow">Met Office: Climate Guide</a> – UK National Weather Service</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://edgcm.columbia.edu/" rel="nofollow">Educational Global Climate Modelling</a> (EdGCM) – research-quality climate change simulator</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www-pcmdi.llnl.gov/projects/pcmdi/index.php" rel="nofollow">Program for Climate Model Diagnosis and Intercomparison</a> – develops and releases standardized models such as CMIP3 (AR4) and CMIP5 (AR5)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Educational">Educational</span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://climate.nasa.gov/evidence/" rel="nofollow">NASA: Climate change: How do we know?</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://climate.jpl.nasa.gov/" rel="nofollow">Global Climate Change: NASA's Eyes on the Earth</a> – NASA, JPL, Caltech</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.ncdc.noaa.gov/indicators/" rel="nofollow">Global Climate Change Indicators</a> – NOAA</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.climate.gov/#understandingClimate" rel="nofollow">NOAA Climate Services</a> – NOAA</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://nsidc.org" rel="nofollow">Sea Ice news</a> – National Snow and Ice Data Center (NSIDC)</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.skepticalscience.com/" rel="nofollow">Skeptical Science: Getting skeptical about global warming skepticism</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://www2.ucar.edu/global-warming-climate-change/faq" rel="nofollow">Understanding Climate Change – Frequently Asked Questions</a> – UCAR</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.jpl.nasa.gov/news/news.php?feature=6701" rel="nofollow">Global Carbon Dioxide Circulation</a> (<a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>; December 13, 2016)</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.worldbank.org/en/news/feature/2012/11/18/Climate-change-report-warns-dramatically-warmer-world-this-century" rel="nofollow">The World Bank – Climate Change – A 4 Degree Warmer World – We must and can avoid it</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=lft4OHt0-gE" rel="nofollow">A world with this much CO²: lessons from 4 million years ago</a> (Video)</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZGFAWzjO378" rel="nofollow">The 8 Minute Epoch: 65 million Years with James Hansen</a> (Video)</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=3UVb--2-PBg" rel="nofollow">Richard Alley: "The Biggest Control Knob: Carbon Dioxide in Earth's Climate History"</a> (Video)</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://geology.com/sea-level-rise/" rel="nofollow">Global Sea Level Rise Map</a></li>
